Baker</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="description" style="text-align:center;background-color:  #E6E8FA;"><i><a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">A Night at the Opera</a></i> <span class="nowrap">track listing</span></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left">\n<div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="box-sizing:border-box;width:100%;font-size:95%;padding:4px;border:none;"><div style="font-size:100%;line-height:1.6;font-weight:bold;background:transparent;text-align:center;;">12 tracks</div><div class="mw-collapsible-content" style="background:transparent;text-align:left;;">\n<dl><dt>Side one</dt></dl>\n<ol><li>"<a href="/wiki/Death_on_Two_Legs_(Dedicated_to...)" title="Death on Two Legs (Dedicated to...)">Death on Two Legs (Dedicated to...)</a>"</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/Lazing_on_a_Sunday_Afternoon" title="Lazing on a Sunday Afternoon">Lazing on a Sunday Afternoon</a>"</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/I%27m_in_Love_with_My_Car" title="I&#39;m in Love with My Car">I\'m in Love with My Car</a>"</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/You%27re_My_Best_Friend_(Queen_song)" title="You&#39;re My Best Friend (Queen song)">You\'re My Best Friend</a>"</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/%2739" title="&#39;39">\'39</a>"</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/Sweet_Lady_(Queen_song)" title="Sweet Lady (Queen song)">Sweet Lady</a>"</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/Seaside_Rendezvous" title="Seaside Rendezvous">Seaside Rendezvous</a>"</li></ol>\n<dl><dt>Side two</dt></dl>\n<ol><li class="mw-empty-elt"></li><li value="8">"<a href="/wiki/The_Prophet%27s_Song" title="The Prophet&#39;s Song">The Prophet\'s Song</a>"</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/Love_of_My_Life_(Queen_song)" title="Love of My Life (Queen song)">Love of My Life</a>"</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/Good_Company_(Queen_song)" title="Good Company (Queen song)">Good Company</a>"</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/Bohemian_Rhapsody" title="Bohemian Rhapsody">Bohemian Rhapsody</a>"</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/A_Night_at_the_Opera_(Queen_album)#&quot;God_Save_the_Queen&quot;" title="A Night at the Opera (Queen album)">God Save the Queen</a>"</li></ol></div></div>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In 1977, the <a href="/wiki/Sex_Pistols" title="Sex Pistols">Sex Pistols</a> recorded a song titled "<a href="/wiki/God_Save_the_Queen_(Sex_Pistols_song)" title="God Save the Queen (Sex Pistols song)">God Save the Queen</a>" in open reference to the National Anthem and the <a href="/wiki/Silver_Jubilee_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Silver Jubilee of Elizabeth II">Queen\'s Silver Jubilee celebrations</a> that year, with the song intending to stand for sympathy for the working class and resentment of the monarchy.<sup id="cite_ref-SPIST_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPIST-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> They were banned from many venues, censored by mainstream media, and reached number 2 on the official U.K. singles charts and number 1 on the NME chart.<sup id="cite_ref-SPIST_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPIST-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A version of "God Save the Queen" by <a href="/wiki/Madness_(band)" title="Madness (band)">Madness</a> features the melody of the song played on <a href="/wiki/Kazoo" title="Kazoo">kazoos</a>. It was included on the compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/The_Business_%E2%80%93_the_Definitive_Singles_Collection" title="The Business \xe2\x80\x93 the Definitive Singles Collection">The Business \xe2\x80\x93 the Definitive Singles Collection</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Composer <a href="/wiki/Steve_Ouimette" title="Steve Ouimette">Steve Ouimette</a> recorded a rock version as downloadable content for the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Guitar_Hero_5" title="Guitar Hero 5">Guitar Hero 5</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Canadian rocker <a href="/wiki/Neil_Young" title="Neil Young">Neil Young</a> recorded a rock version of "God Save the Queen", merged with "America (My Country \'Tis of Thee)", for his 2012 <a href="/wiki/Americana_(Neil_Young_%26_Crazy_Horse_album)" title="Americana (Neil Young &amp; Crazy Horse album)">Americana</a> album with <a href="/wiki/Crazy_Horse_(band)" title="Crazy Horse (band)">Crazy Horse</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=God_Save_the_Queen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The title is <i>Dog Save the Queen</i>, from <i><a href="/wiki/T.U.F.F._Puppy" title="T.U.F.F. Puppy">T.U.F.F. Puppy</a></i>\n</p><p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Team_Fortress_2" title="Team Fortress 2">Team Fortress 2</a></i>, one of the Sniper\'s quotes is the same title as the anthem. This is in reference to New Zealand (the Sniper\'s birthplace) being a former British colony.\n</p><p>In the movie version of <i><a href="/wiki/V_for_Vendetta" title="V for Vendetta">V for Vendetta</a></i> during an episode of Gordon Deitrich\'s show, which sends up Chancellor Adam Suttler.\n</p><p>In \'The Royal Canadian Kilted Yaksmen\' episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Ren_%26_Stimpy" class="mw-redirect" title="Ren &amp; Stimpy">Ren &amp; Stimpy</a></i> (the song is the Royal Canadian Kilted Yaksmen anthem.)\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Computer_music">Computer music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=God_Save_the_Queen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Computer music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The anthem was the first piece of music played on a computer, and the first computer music to be recorded.\n</p><p>Musical notes were first generated by a computer programmed by <a href="/wiki/Alan_Turing" title="Alan Turing">Alan Turing</a> at the Computing Machine Laboratory of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Manchester" title="University of Manchester">University of Manchester</a> in 1948. The first music proper, a performance of the National Anthem was programmed by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Strachey" title="Christopher Strachey">Christopher Strachey</a> on the Mark II <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Electronic_Computer" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Electronic Computer">Manchester Electronic Computer</a> at same venue, in 1951. Later that year, short extracts of three pieces, the first being the National Anthem, were recorded there by a <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> outside broadcasting unit: the other pieces being "<a href="/wiki/Ba_Ba_Black_Sheep" class="mw-redirect" title="Ba Ba Black Sheep">Ba Ba Black Sheep</a>, and "<a href="/wiki/In_the_Mood" title="In the Mood">In the Mood</a>". Researchers at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Canterbury" title="University of Canterbury">University of Canterbury</a>, Christchurch restored the acetate master disc in 2016 and the results may be heard on <a href="/wiki/Soundcloud" class="mw-redirect" title="Soundcloud">Soundcloud</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Turing_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turing-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BL-2016-09_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BL-2016-09-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=God_Save_the_Queen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The philosopher and reformer <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Bentham" title="Jeremy Bentham">Jeremy Bentham</a> praised "God Save the King" in 1796: "the melody recommending itself by beauty to the most polished ears, and by its simplicity to the rudest ear. A song of this complexion, implanted by the habit of half a century in the mass of popular sentiment, can not be refused a place in the inventory of the national blessings."<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Ludwig van Beethoven wrote "I have to show the English a little of what a blessing \'God Save the King\' is".<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Alex Marshall, the British author of <i>Republic or Death!: Travels in Search of National Anthems</i>, called the anthem "ludicrous".<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Calls_for_a_new_national_anthem.2Fanthems"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Calls_for_a_new_national_anthem/anthems">Calls for a new national anthem/anthems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=God_Save_the_Queen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Calls for a new national anthem/anthems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There have been calls within the UK for a new national anthem, whether it be for the United Kingdom itself, Britain and/or England (which all currently use God Save the Queen). There are many reasons people cite for wishing for a new national anthem, such as: from a non-religious standpoint<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> (the majority of people in the UK today identify as not religious),<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> claims of God Save the Queen being long outdated and irrelevant in the 21st century,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> rejection of odes to promoting war<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> and rejection of praising the monarchy from a <a href="/wiki/Republicanism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Republicanism in the United Kingdom">republican</a> perspective.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>  A further reason is that <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> has no anthem of its own for sporting contests and the like, whereas <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> do; <a href="/wiki/Flower_of_Scotland" title="Flower of Scotland">Flower of Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Londonderry_Air" title="Londonderry Air">Londonderry Air</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Land_of_My_Fathers" class="mw-redirect" title="Land of My Fathers">Land of My Fathers</a> fill this niche (the former two on an unofficial basis), while England tends to use <i>God Save the Queen</i> exclusively and also unofficially.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=God_Save_the_Queen&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
